**Result:**

     1→# Code Correctness Report: types-and-lib  
     2→  
     3→**Agent:** epcp-code-correctness-agent  
     4→**Domain:** types-and-lib  
     5→**Files audited:** 10  
     6→**Date:** 2026-02-17T00:18:00Z  
     7→  
     8→## MUST-FIX  
     9→  
    10→### [CC-001] task-registry.ts: No file locking on write operations — race condition  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:95,132,179  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** race-condition  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `createTask()`, `updateTask()`, and `deleteTask()` all perform read-modify-write sequences (`loadTasks` -> mutate -> `saveTasks`) without any file locking. Unlike `team-registry.ts`, `transfer-registry.ts`, and `governance.ts`, which all use `withLock()` from `@/lib/file-lock`, `task-registry.ts` does not import or use `withLock` at all. Two concurrent API requests to create/update/delete tasks on the same team will race: both read the same file, mutate independently, and the second write silently overwrites the first, losing data.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // lib/task-registry.ts — NO withLock anywhere in this file  
    19→  export function createTask(data: { teamId: string; ... }): Task {  
    20→    const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)  // READ  
    21→    // ... build task ...  
    22→    tasks.push(task)                       // MUTATE  
    23→    saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)          // WRITE — can overwrite concurrent changes  
    24→    return task  
    25→  }  
    26→  ```  
    27→  Compare with `team-registry.ts` which wraps every write in `withLock('teams', () => { ... })`.  
    28→- **Fix:** Import `withLock` from `@/lib/file-lock` and wrap `createTask`, `updateTask`, and `deleteTask` in `withLock('tasks-' + teamId, ...)`. This requires making them `async` (matching the pattern in `team-registry.ts`). Note: `wouldCreateCycle` is read-only and does not need locking.  
    29→  
    30→## SHOULD-FIX  
    31→  

... [10731 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    10→### [CC-001] `params` type mismatch in agent transfer route (non-Promise in Next.js 14.2)  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/agents/[id]/transfer/route.ts:33  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** type-safety  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** The route handler uses `{ params }: { params: { id: string } }` and accesses `params.id` synchronously at line 37. Every other `[id]` route in this codebase (40+ occurrences) uses `{ params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }` with `const { id } = await params`. This project runs Next.js 14.2.35 where params is a Promise in App Router route handlers. Synchronous access works today because Next.js resolves it internally, but it emits a deprecation warning and will break in Next.js 15.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // Line 31-37 of transfer/route.ts  
    19→  export async function POST(  
    20→    request: Request,  
    21→    { params }: { params: { id: string } }  // <-- non-Promise  
    22→  ) {  
    23→    try {  
    24→      let agent = getAgent(params.id)  // <-- synchronous access  
    25→  ```  
    26→  vs. all other routes:  
    27→  ```typescript  
    28→  // Example from resolve/route.ts line 14-19  
    29→  export async function POST(  
    30→    request: NextRequest,  
    31→    { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  // <-- Promise  
    32→  ) {  
    33→    const { id } = await params  // <-- awaited  
    34→  ```  
    35→- **Fix:** Change type to `Promise<{ id: string }>` and add `const { id } = await params` at the top of the function. Also change `Request` to `NextRequest` for consistency.  
    36→  
    37→### [CC-002] Transfer approval creates inconsistent state when destination team i  

... [12794 more chars truncated]

    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/teams/[id]/tasks/[taskId]/route.ts:93-114  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** logic  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The DELETE handler does not wrap its body in a try/catch block. If `await params`, `getTeam()`, `checkTeamAccess()`, or `deleteTask()` throw an unexpected exception, Next.js will return an opaque 500 error with no JSON body. The PUT handler in the same file has a try/catch, so this is an inconsistency within the same route file.  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→```typescript  
    22→// Line 93-114: No try/catch  
    23→export async function DELETE(  
    24→  request: NextRequest,  
    25→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string; taskId: string }> }  
    26→) {  
    27→  const { id, taskId } = await params  
    28→  const team = getTeam(id)  
    29→  // ... no error boundary ...  
    30→  const deleted = deleteTask(id, taskId)  
    31→  if (!deleted) {  
    32→    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Task not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    33→  }  
    34→  return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    35→}  
    36→```  
    37→- **Fix:** Wrap the DELETE handler body in a try/catch with a `console.error` and a 500 JSON response, matching the pattern used in the PUT handler.  
    38→  
    39→### [CC-002] Missing try/catch in GET /api/teams/[id]/tasks

    14→### [CC-001] Race condition: stale `refresh()` response when `agentId` changes rapidly  
    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useGovernance.ts:63-100  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** race-condition  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The `refresh` callback fires three parallel fetches and unconditionally writes results to state. If `agentId` changes while fetches are in-flight (e.g., user clicks between agents quickly), the older fetch's `.then()` handler will overwrite state with data that no longer matches the current `agentId`. Because `refresh` is re-created via `useCallback([agentId])`, the old closure's `setLoading`/`setAllTeams`/etc. still reference the same state setters. There is no cancellation (AbortController) and no staleness guard (e.g., checking a ref against current agentId before calling setState).  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→  ```typescript  
    22→  // Line 63-100  
    23→  const refresh = useCallback(() => {  
    24→    setLoading(true)  
    25→    Promise.all([  
    26→      fetch('/api/governance').then(...)  // <-- no AbortController  
    27→      fetch('/api/teams').then(...)  
    28→      fetch('/api/governance/transfers?status=pending').then(...)  
    29→    ])  
    30→      .then(([govData, teamsData, transfersData]) => {  
    31→        // These run even if agentId changed since the fetch started  
    32→        setHasPassword(govData.hasPassword ?? false)  
    33→        setAllTeams(teamsData.teams ?? [])  
    34→        setPendingTransfers(transfersData.requests ?? [])  
    35→      })  
    36→      ...  
    37→  }, [agentId])  
    38→  ```

    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/scripts/remote-install.sh:1225  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** shell  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED (tested on macOS)  
    19→- **Description:** The `gw_list` variable is built with literal `\n` strings (shell does not expand `\n` in double-quoted string assignment). When `portable_sed` substitutes `{{ACTIVE_GATEWAYS_LIST}}` in MAILMAN-CLAUDE.md, the result is a single line containing `- Slack\n- Discord` literally, rather than separate lines with actual newlines. The template at `scripts/MAILMAN-CLAUDE.md:14` expects a multi-line bullet list.  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→```bash  
    22→# Line 1224-1225:  
    23→if [ -n "$gw_list" ]; then  
    24→    gw_list="${gw_list}\n- ${gw_display}"  
    25→```  
    26→On macOS, `"${gw_list}\n- ${gw_display}"` produces the literal string `- Slack\n- Discord`, not `- Slack` + newline + `- Discord`.  
    27→- **Fix:** Use `$'\n'` for actual newlines, or use `printf` to build the string:  
    28→```bash  
    29→gw_list="${gw_list}"$'\n'"- ${gw_display}"  
    30→```  
    31→Or alternatively use `printf '%s\n' "- ${gw_display}"` to append to the variable.

     7→  
     8→## MUST-FIX  
     9→  
    10→### [CC-001] task-registry.ts: No file locking on write operations — race condition  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:95,132,179  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** race-condition  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `createTask()`, `updateTask()`, and `deleteTask()` all perform read-modify-write sequences (`loadTasks` -> mutate -> `saveTasks`) without any file locking. Unlike `team-registry.ts`, `transfer-registry.ts`, and `governance.ts`, which all use `withLock()` from `@/lib/file-lock`, `task-registry.ts` does not import or use `withLock` at all. Two concurrent API requests to create/update/delete tasks on the same team will race: both read the same file, mutate independently, and the second write silently overwrites the first, losing data.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // lib/task-registry.ts — NO withLock anywhere in this file  
    19→  export function createTask(data: { teamId: string; ... }): Task {  
    20→    const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)  // READ  
    21→    // ... build task ...  
    22→    tasks.push(task)                       // MUTATE  
    23→    saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)          // WRITE — can overwrite concurrent changes  
    24→    return task  
    25→  }  
    26→  ```  
    27→  Compare with `team-registry.ts` which wraps every write in `withLock('teams', () => { ... })`.  
    28→- **Fix:** Import `withLock` from `@/lib/file-lock` and wrap `createTask`, `updateTask`, and `deleteTask` in `withLock('tasks-' + teamId, ...)`. This requires making them `async` (matching the pattern in `team-registry.ts`). Note: `wouldCreateCycle` is read-only and does not need locking.  
    29→  
    30→## SHOULD-FIX  
    31→  

... [10731 more chars truncated]

    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/agents/[id]/transfer/route.ts:33  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** type-safety  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** The route handler uses `{ params }: { params: { id: string } }` and accesses `params.id` synchronously at line 37. Every other `[id]` route in this codebase (40+ occurrences) uses `{ params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }` with `const { id } = await params`. This project runs Next.js 14.2.35 where params is a Promise in App Router route handlers. Synchronous access works today because Next.js resolves it internally, but it emits a deprecation warning and will break in Next.js 15.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // Line 31-37 of transfer/route.ts  
    19→  export async function POST(  
    20→    request: Request,

    22→  ) {  
    23→    try {  
    24→      let agent = getAgent(params.id)  // <-- synchronous access  
    25→  ```  
    26→  vs. all other routes:  
    27→  ```typescript  
    28→  // Example from resolve/route.ts line 14-19  
    29→  export async function POST(  
    30→    request: NextRequest,  
    31→    { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  // <-- Promise  
    32→  ) {  
    33→    const { id } = await params  // <-- awaited  
    34→  ```  
    35→- **Fix:** Change type to `Promise<{ id: string }>` and add `const { id } = await params` at the top of the function. Also change `Request` to `NextRequest` for consistency.

  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { loadGovernance } from './governance'  
    11→import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    14→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    15→  recipientAgentId: string  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }  
    45→  
    46→  // Single snapshot of all state — avoids redundant file reads from

   117→      return { valid: false, error: `Invalid team type: "${data.type}" (must be "open" or "closed")`, code: 400 }  
   118→    }  
   119→  }  
   120→  
   121→  // Resolve effective state after this mutation is applied  
   122→  const existingTeam = teamId ? teams.find(t => t.id === teamId) : null  
   123→  const effectiveType = (data.type ?? existingTeam?.type ?? 'open') as string  
   124→  const effectiveCOS = data.chiefOfStaffId !== undefined ? data.chiefOfStaffId : (existingTeam?.chiefOfStaffId ?? null)  
   125→  const effectiveAgentIds = data.agentIds ?? existingTeam?.agentIds ?? []  
   126→  
   127→  // --- COS-Closed Invariant (R1.3, R1.4) ---  
   128→  if (effectiveType === 'closed' && !effectiveCOS) {  
   129→    return { valid: false, error: 'A closed team must have a Chief-of-Staff assigned', code: 400 }  
   130→  }  
   131→  // --- COS on open team is invalid (R1.8) ---  
   132→  if (effectiveType === 'open' && effectiveCOS) {  
   133→    return { valid: false, error: 'Cannot assign a Chief-of-Staff to an open team (change type to closed first)', code: 400 }  
   134→  }  
   135→

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [474 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     3→  
     4→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     5→  try {  
     6→    const body = await request.json()  
     7→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     8→  
     9→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    10→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    11→    }  
    12→  
    13→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    14→  
    15→    // If password already set, require current password  
    16→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    17→      if (!currentPassword || !verifyPassword(currentPassword)) {  
    18→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    19→      }  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    const isChange = !!config.passwordHash  
    23→    await setPassword(password)  
    24→  
    25→    if (isChange) {  
    26→      console.log('[governance] Password changed at', new Date().toISOString())  
    27→    } else {  
    28→      console.log('[governance] Password set at', new Date().toISOString())  
    29→    }  
    30→  
    31→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    32→  } catch (error) {  
    33→    console.error('Failed to set password:', error)  
    34→    return NextResponse.json(  
    35→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set password' },  
    36→      { status: 500 }  
    37→    )  
    38→  }  
    39→}

     8→## MUST-FIX  
     9→  
    10→### [CC-001] task-registry.ts: No file locking on write operations — race condition  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:95,132,179  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** race-condition  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `createTask()`, `updateTask()`, and `deleteTask()` all perform read-modify-write sequences (`loadTasks` -> mutate -> `saveTasks`) without any file locking. Unlike `team-registry.ts`, `transfer-registry.ts`, and `governance.ts`, which all use `withLock()` from `@/lib/file-lock`, `task-registry.ts` does not import or use `withLock` at all. Two concurrent API requests to create/update/delete tasks on the same team will race: both read the same file, mutate independently, and the second write silently overwrites the first, losing data.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // lib/task-registry.ts — NO withLock anywhere in this file  
    19→  export function createTask(data: { teamId: string; ... }): Task {  
    20→    const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)  // READ  
    21→    // ... build task ...  
    22→    tasks.push(task)                       // MUTATE  
    23→    saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)          // WRITE — can overwrite concurrent changes  
    24→    return task  
    25→  }  
    26→  ```  
    27→  Compare with `team-registry.ts` which wraps every write in `withLock('teams', () => { ... })`.  
    28→- **Fix:** Import `withLock` from `@/lib/file-lock` and wrap `createTask`, `updateTask`, and `deleteTask` in `withLock('tasks-' + teamId, ...)`. This requires making them `async` (matching the pattern in `team-registry.ts`). Note: `wouldCreateCycle` is read-only and does not need locking.  
    29→  
    30→## SHOULD-FIX  
    31→  

... [10731 more chars truncated]

    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX

    15→- **Description:** The route handler uses `{ params }: { params: { id: string } }` and accesses `params.id` synchronously at line 37. Every other `[id]` route in this codebase (40+ occurrences) uses `{ params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }` with `const { id } = await params`. This project runs Next.js 14.2.35 where params is a Promise in App Router route handlers. Synchronous access works today because Next.js resolves it internally, but it emits a deprecation warning and will break in Next.js 15.  
    16→- **Evidence:**

    22→  ) {  
    23→    try {  
    24→      let agent = getAgent(params.id)  // <-- synchronous access  
    25→  ```  
    26→  vs. all other routes:  
    27→  ```typescript  
    28→  // Example from resolve/route.ts line 14-19  
    29→  export async function POST(  
    30→    request: NextRequest,  
    31→    { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  // <-- Promise  
    32→  ) {  
    33→    const { id } = await params  // <-- awaited  
    34→  ```  
    35→- **Fix:** Change type to `Promise<{ id: string }>` and add `const { id } = await params` at the top of the function. Also change `Request` to `NextRequest` for consistency.

    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useGovernance.ts:63-100  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** race-condition  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The `refresh` callback fires three parallel fetches and unconditionally writes results to state. If `agentId` changes while fetches are in-flight (e.g., user clicks between agents quickly), the older fetch's `.then()` handler will overwrite state with data that no longer matches the current `agentId`. Because `refresh` is re-created via `useCallback([agentId])`, the old closure's `setLoading`/`setAllTeams`/etc. still reference the same state setters. There is no cancellation (AbortController) and no staleness guard (e.g., checking a ref against current agentId before calling setState).

    34→        setPendingTransfers(transfersData.requests ?? [])  
    35→      })  
    36→      ...  
    37→  }, [agentId])  
    38→  ```

    35→ */  
    36→export function sanitizeTeamName(raw: string): string {  
    37→  return raw  
    38→    .replace(/[\x00-\x1F\x7F]/g, '')  // Strip control characters (same as agent name sanitization)  
    39→    .replace(/\s+/g, ' ')              // Collapse all whitespace into single space  
    40→    .trim()  
    41→}

     7→import { getTransferRequest, resolveTransferRequest } from '@/lib/transfer-registry'  
     8→import { loadTeams, saveTeams, TeamValidationException } from '@/lib/team-registry'

    11→import { notifyAgent } from '@/lib/notification-service'

    13→  
    14→export async function POST(  
    15→  request: NextRequest,  
    16→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    17→) {  
    18→  try {  
    19→    const { id } = await params  
    20→    const body = await request.json()  
    21→    const { action, resolvedBy, rejectReason } = body  
    22→  
    23→    if (!action || !resolvedBy) {  
    24→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'action and resolvedBy are required' }, { status: 400 })  
    25→    }  
    26→    if (action !== 'approve' && action !== 'reject') {  
    27→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'action must be "approve" or "reject"' }, { status: 400 })  
    28→    }  
    29→  
    30→    // Get the transfer request  
    31→    const transferReq = getTransferRequest(id)  
    32→    if (!transferReq) {  
    33→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Transfer request not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    34→    }  
    35→    if (transferReq.status !== 'pending') {  
    36→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Transfer request is already resolved' }, { status: 409 })  
    37→    }  
    38→  
    39→    // Acquire teams lock for the entire read-validate-write cycle to prevent TOCTOU races.  
    40→    // We use acquireLock directly (instead of withLock) because we need to return  
    41→    // NextResponse objects from within the critical section.  
    42→    const releaseLock

     4→import type { Team } from '@/types/team'

     6→interface UseTeamResult {

    14→export function useTeam(teamId: string | null): UseTeamResult {  
    15→  const [team, setTeam] = useState<Team | null>(null)  
    16→  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true)  
    17→  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null)  
    18→  
    19→  const fetchTeam = useCallback(async () => {  
    20→    if (!teamId) return  
    21→    try {  
    22→      const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`)  
    23→      if (!res.ok) throw new Error('Failed to fetch team')  
    24→      const data = await res.json()  
    25→      setTeam(data.team || null)  
    26→      setError(null)  
    27→    } catch (err) {  
    28→      setError(err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to fetch team')  
    29→    }  
    30→  }, [teamId])  
    31→  
    32→  // Initial fetch  
    33→  useEffect(() => {  
    34→    if (!teamId) {  
    35→      setTeam(null)  
    36→      setLoading(false)  
    37→      return  
    38→    }  
    39→    setLoading(true)  
    40→    fetchTeam().finally(() => setLoading(false))  
    41→  }, [teamId, fetchTeam])  
    42→  
    43→  const updateTeam = useCallback(async (updates: { name?: string; description?: string; agentIds?: string[]; instructions?: string }) => {  
    44→    if (!teamId) return  
    45→    // Optimistic update  
    46→    setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...updates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)  
    47→    const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`, {  
    48→      method: 'PUT',  
    49→      headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },  
    50→      body: JSON.stringify({

     2→# AI Maestro - Version Bump Script  
     3→# Centralizes version management across all files  
     4→#  
     5→# Usage:  
     6→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh patch    # 0.17.12 -> 0.17.13  
     7→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh minor    # 0.17.12 -> 0.18.0  
     8→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh major    # 0.17.12 -> 1.0.0  
     9→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh 0.18.0   # Set specific version

   164→  const addAgentToTeam = useCallback(  
   165→    async (teamId: string, targetAgentId: string): Promise<{ success: boolean; error?: string }> => {  
   166→      try {  
   167→        // Note: This performs a client-side read-modify-write across two HTTP requests.  
   168→        // Concurrent modifications from multiple tabs may lose updates.  
   169→        // Server-side withLock protects file integrity but not HTTP-level atomicity.  
   170→        // Acceptable for Phase 1 (single user, localhost). TODO: atomic endpoint for Phase 2.  
   171→  
   172→        // Fetch current team to get existing agentIds  
   173→        const teamRes = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`)  
   174→        if (!teamRes.ok) return { success: false, error: 'Failed to fetch team' }  
   175→        const teamData = await teamRes.json()  
   176→        const team: Team = teamData.team  
   177→  
   178→        // Add agent if not already present  
   179→        const updatedAgentIds = team.agentIds.includes(targetAgentId)  
   180→          ? team.agentIds  
   181→          : [...team.agentIds, targetAgentId]

```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

   127→export function getTask(teamId: string, taskId: string): Task | null {
